  <div id="scenarios-q14" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q14-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">
    <div class="accordion-body">
      <p><strong>Library choice:</strong></p>
      <ul>
        <li><strong>Recharts</strong> — React-first, declarative, good for standard charts.</li>
        <li><strong>Victory</strong> — composable, animatable.</li>
        <li><strong>D3.js</strong> — maximum flexibility, custom/exotic chart types.</li>
        <li><strong>Chart.js + react-chartjs-2</strong> — canvas-based, performant for many points.</li>
      </ul>
<pre class="code-block">// Recharts example — responsive line chart with real-time data
import {
  LineChart, Line, XAxis, YAxis, CartesianGrid,
  Tooltip, Legend, ResponsiveContainer
} from 'recharts';

function MetricsChart({ data }: { data: MetricPoint[] }) {
  return (
    &lt;ResponsiveContainer width="100%" height={300}&gt;
      &lt;LineChart data={data}&gt;
        &lt;CartesianGrid strokeDasharray="3 3" /&gt;
        &lt;XAxis dataKey="timestamp"
          tickFormatter={ts =&gt; new Date(ts).toLocaleTimeString()} /&gt;
        &lt;YAxis /&gt;
        &lt;Tooltip /&gt;
        &lt;Legend /&gt;
        &lt;Line type="monotone" dataKey="value" stroke="#8884d8"
          dot={false} isAnimationActive={false} /&gt;
      &lt;/LineChart&gt;
    &lt;/ResponsiveContainer&gt;
  );
}

// For real-time: disable animation, limit data window
function LiveChart() {
  const [points, setPoints] = useState&lt;MetricPoint[]&gt;([]);

  useEffect(() =&gt; {
    const unsub = subscribeToMetrics(point =&gt; {
      setPoints(prev =&gt; [...prev.slice(-100), point]); // keep last 100 points
    });
    return unsub;
  }, []);

  return &lt;MetricsChart data={points} /&gt;;
}</pre>
      <p><strong>D3 + React pattern:</strong> Use D3 only for math/scale/path calculations; let React own the DOM. This avoids the D3 vs React DOM ownership conflict. Use refs only when D3 must own the DOM (e.g., drag/zoom behaviors).</p>
      <p><strong>Accessibility:</strong> Add <code>role="img"</code> and <code>aria-label</code> to chart containers. Provide a data table fallback for screen reader users.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

<!-- Q15 -->
<div class="accordion-item">
  <h2 class="accordion-header" id="scenarios-q15-heading">
    <button class="accordion-button collapsed" type="button" data-bs-toggle="collapse" data-bs-target="#scenarios-q15" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="scenarios-q15">
      <span class="diff-scenario">Scenario</span>&nbsp; 15. How would you implement a dark mode toggle that persists?
    </button>
  </h2>
  <div id="scenarios-q15" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q15-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">
    <div class="accordion-body">
      <p><strong>Approach — CSS variables + class on root element:</strong></p>
<pre class="code-block">// theme-context.tsx
type Theme = 'light' | 'dark';

function getInitialTheme(): Theme {
  const stored = localStorage.getItem('theme') as Theme | null;
  if (stored) return stored;
  return window.matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: dark)').matches ? 'dark' : 'light';
}

export function ThemeProvider({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState&lt;Theme&gt;(getInitialTheme);

  useEffect(() =&gt; {
    document.documentElement.classList.toggle('dark', theme === 'dark');
    localStorage.setItem('theme', theme);
  }, [theme]);

  // Also respond to OS-level changes
  useEffect(() =&gt; {
    const mq = window.matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: dark)');
    const handler = (e: MediaQueryListEvent) =&gt;
      setTheme(e.matches ? 'dark' : 'light');
    mq.addEventListener('change', handler);
    return () =&gt; mq.removeEventListener('change', handler);
  }, []);

  return (
    &lt;ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, toggle: () =&gt;
      setTheme(t =&gt; t === 'dark' ? 'light' : 'dark') }}&gt;
      {children}
    &lt;/ThemeContext.Provider&gt;
  );
}

/* globals.css */
:root { --bg: #ffffff; --text: #000000; }
:root.dark { --bg: #1a1a1a; --text: #ffffff; }
body { background: var(--bg); color: var(--text); }</pre>
      <p><strong>Tailwind approach:</strong> Set <code>darkMode: 'class'</code> in tailwind.config; toggle <code>class="dark"</code> on <code>&lt;html&gt;</code>. Components use <code>dark:bg-gray-900</code> etc.</p>
      <p><strong>MUI approach:</strong> Pass a dynamic <code>theme</code> object to <code>ThemeProvider</code> based on the mode state. MUI respects <code>createTheme({ palette: { mode: 'dark' } })</code>.</p>
      <p><strong>Flash prevention:</strong> Inline a blocking script in <code>&lt;head&gt;</code> before React hydrates to read localStorage and set the class synchronously — prevents a flash of the wrong theme on page load.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

<!-- Q16 -->
<div class="accordion-item">
  <h2 class="accordion-header" id="scenarios-q16-heading">
    <button class="accordion-button collapsed" type="button" data-bs-toggle="collapse" data-bs-target="#scenarios-q16" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="scenarios-q16">
      <span class="diff-scenario">Scenario</span>&nbsp; 16. How would you build a responsive navigation with mobile drawer?
    </button>
  </h2>
  <div id="scenarios-q16" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q16-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">
    <div class="accordion-body">
      <p><strong>Pattern:</strong> Horizontal nav on desktop; hamburger + slide-in drawer on mobile. Use a <code>useMediaQuery</code> hook or CSS to determine layout.</p>
<pre class="code-block">function useMediaQuery(query: string) {
  const [matches, setMatches] = useState(() =&gt; window.matchMedia(query).matches);
  useEffect(() =&gt; {
    const mq = window.matchMedia(query);
    const handler = (e: MediaQueryListEvent) =&gt; setMatches(e.matches);
    mq.addEventListener('change', handler);
    return () =&gt; mq.removeEventListener('change', handler);
  }, [query]);
  return matches;
}

function Navigation() {
  const isMobile = useMediaQuery('(max-width: 768px)');
  const [drawerOpen, setDrawerOpen] = useState(false);

  const navLinks = [
    { label: 'Home', path: '/' },
    { label: 'Products', path: '/products' },
    { label: 'About', path: '/about' },
  ];

  if (isMobile) return (
    &lt;&gt;
      &lt;button aria-label="Open menu" onClick={() =&gt; setDrawerOpen(true)}&gt;☰&lt;/button&gt;
      {drawerOpen &amp;&amp; (
        &lt;&gt;
          &lt;div className="drawer-backdrop" onClick={() =&gt; setDrawerOpen(false)} /&gt;
          &lt;nav className="drawer" role="navigation" aria-label="Mobile navigation"&gt;
            &lt;button aria-label="Close menu" onClick={() =&gt; setDrawerOpen(false)}&gt;✕&lt;/button&gt;
            {navLinks.map(l =&gt; &lt;Link key={l.path} to={l.path}
              onClick={() =&gt; setDrawerOpen(false)}&gt;{l.label}&lt;/Link&gt;)}
          &lt;/nav&gt;
        &lt;/&gt;
      )}
    &lt;/&gt;
  );

  return (
    &lt;nav role="navigation" aria-label="Main navigation"&gt;
      {navLinks.map(l =&gt; &lt;Link key={l.path} to={l.path}&gt;{l.label}&lt;/Link&gt;)}
    &lt;/nav&gt;
  );
}</pre>
      <p><strong>Accessibility:</strong> Drawer must trap focus when open. Close on <kbd>Escape</kbd>. Return focus to the hamburger button on close. Set <code>aria-expanded</code> on the toggle button.</p>
      <p><strong>Animation:</strong> Use CSS transitions on <code>transform: translateX</code> for the drawer slide-in. Render the drawer in a portal to avoid z-index issues.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

<!-- Q17 -->
<div class="accordion-item">
  <h2 class="accordion-header" id="scenarios-q17-heading">
    <button class="accordion-button collapsed" type="button" data-bs-toggle="collapse" data-bs-target="#scenarios-q17" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="scenarios-q17">
      <span class="diff-scenario">Scenario</span>&nbsp; 17. How would you implement a permissions/role-based access control system?
    </button>
  </h2>
  <div id="scenarios-q17" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q17-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">
    <div class="accordion-body">
      <p><strong>RBAC model:</strong> Users have one or more roles; roles have permissions; components/routes check permissions.</p>
<pre class="code-block">// permissions.ts
export const PERMISSIONS = {
  VIEW_REPORTS: 'view:reports',
  EDIT_USERS: 'edit:users',
  DELETE_ITEMS: 'delete:items',
} as const;

const ROLE_PERMISSIONS: Record&lt;string, string[]&gt; = {
  admin: ['view:reports', 'edit:users', 'delete:items'],
  manager: ['view:reports'],
  viewer: [],
};

// auth-context.tsx
function AuthProvider() {
  const { roles } = useUserFromToken(); // decode JWT claims
  const permissions = useMemo(() =&gt;
    new Set(roles.flatMap(r =&gt; ROLE_PERMISSIONS[r] ?? [])), [roles]);

  const can = useCallback((permission: string) =&gt;
    permissions.has(permission), [permissions]);

  return &lt;AuthContext.Provider value={{ roles, can }}&gt;...&lt;/AuthContext.Provider&gt;;
}

// Can component — renders children only if permitted
function Can({ permission, children, fallback = null }: {
  permission: string; children: React.ReactNode; fallback?: React.ReactNode;
}) {
  const { can } = useAuth();
  return can(permission) ? &lt;&gt;{children}&lt;/&gt; : &lt;&gt;{fallback}&lt;/&gt;;
}

// Protected route wrapper
function ProtectedRoute({ permission, children }: { permission: string; children: React.ReactNode }) {
  const { can } = useAuth();
  if (!can(permission)) return &lt;Navigate to="/unauthorized" /&gt;;
  return &lt;&gt;{children}&lt;/&gt;;
}

// Usage
&lt;Can permission={PERMISSIONS.EDIT_USERS}&gt;
  &lt;EditUserButton /&gt;
&lt;/Can&gt;</pre>
      <p><strong>Important:</strong> Frontend RBAC is UX only — the backend must enforce all permissions. Never trust client-side permission checks for security.</p>
      <p><strong>Claim-based approach:</strong> For fine-grained permissions, include a <code>permissions</code> array directly in the JWT rather than deriving from roles, eliminating the need for a client-side role-to-permission mapping.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

<!-- Q18 -->
<div class="accordion-item">
  <h2 class="accordion-header" id="scenarios-q18-heading">
    <button class="accordion-button collapsed" type="button" data-bs-toggle="collapse" data-bs-target="#scenarios-q18" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="scenarios-q18">
      <span class="diff-scenario">Scenario</span>&nbsp; 18. How would you build a form that auto-saves to the server?
    </button>
  </h2>
  <div id="scenarios-q18" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q18-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">
    <div class="accordion-body">
      <p><strong>Strategy:</strong> Debounce field changes and PATCH to server. Track save state to show user feedback.</p>
<pre class="code-block">// useAutosave.ts
type SaveStatus = 'idle' | 'saving' | 'saved' | 'error';

export function useAutosave&lt;T&gt;(
  data: T,
  saveFn: (data: T) =&gt; Promise&lt;void&gt;,
  delay = 1000
) {
  const [status, setStatus] = useState&lt;SaveStatus&gt;('idle');
  const latestData = useRef(data);
  latestData.current = data;

  useEffect(() =&gt; {
    const id = setTimeout(async () =&gt; {
      setStatus('saving');
      try {
        await saveFn(latestData.current);
        setStatus('saved');
        setTimeout(() =&gt; setStatus('idle'), 2000);
      } catch {
        setStatus('error');
      }
    }, delay);
    return () =&gt; clearTimeout(id);
  }, [data, saveFn, delay]); // re-debounces whenever data changes

  return status;
}

// AutoSaveForm.tsx
function DocumentEditor({ docId }: { docId: string }) {
  const [title, setTitle] = useState('');
  const [body, setBody] = useState('');

  const saveDoc = useCallback(
    (data: { title: string; body: string }) =&gt;
      api.patch(`/documents/${docId}`, data),
    [docId]
  );

  const status = useAutosave({ title, body }, saveDoc, 800);

  return (
    &lt;div&gt;
      &lt;div className="save-indicator"&gt;
        {status === 'saving' &amp;&amp; 'Saving...'}
        {status === 'saved' &amp;&amp; 'Saved ✓'}
        {status === 'error' &amp;&amp; 'Save failed'}
      &lt;/div&gt;
      &lt;input value={title} onChange={e =&gt; setTitle(e.target.value)} /&gt;
      &lt;textarea value={body} onChange={e =&gt; setBody(e.target.value)} /&gt;
    &lt;/div&gt;
  );
}</pre>
      <p><strong>Save on unmount:</strong> Use <code>window.beforeunload</code> or a <code>useEffect</code> cleanup that triggers an immediate (non-debounced) save when the component unmounts or the user navigates away.</p>
      <p><strong>Conflict resolution:</strong> Include a version/etag in the PATCH request. If the server returns 409 Conflict, show a merge UI.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

<!-- Q19 -->
<div class="accordion-item">
  <h2 class="accordion-header" id="scenarios-q19-heading">
    <button class="accordion-button collapsed" type="button" data-bs-toggle="collapse" data-bs-target="#scenarios-q19" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="scenarios-q19">
      <span class="diff-scenario">Scenario</span>&nbsp; 19. How would you implement keyboard navigation for accessibility?
    </button>
  </h2>
  <div id="scenarios-q19" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q19-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">
    <div class="accordion-body">
      <p><strong>Core principles:</strong> All interactive elements reachable by Tab, logical focus order, keyboard operable with arrow keys where appropriate, visible focus indicators.</p>
<pre class="code-block">// Custom hook for roving tabindex (arrow key nav in a group)
function useRovingTabIndex(count: number) {
  const [activeIndex, setActiveIndex] = useState(0);
  const refs = useRef&lt;(HTMLElement | null)[]&gt;([]);

  function handleKeyDown(e: React.KeyboardEvent, index: number) {
    let next = index;
    if (e.key === 'ArrowDown' || e.key === 'ArrowRight') {
      e.preventDefault();
      next = (index + 1) % count;
    } else if (e.key === 'ArrowUp' || e.key === 'ArrowLeft') {
      e.preventDefault();
      next = (index - 1 + count) % count;
    } else if (e.key === 'Home') {
      next = 0;
    } else if (e.key === 'End') {
      next = count - 1;
    }
    setActiveIndex(next);
    refs.current[next]?.focus();
  }

  function getTabIndex(index: number) {
    return index === activeIndex ? 0 : -1;
  }

  return { getTabIndex, handleKeyDown, refs };
}

// Accessible toolbar using roving tabindex
function Toolbar({ tools }: { tools: Tool[] }) {
  const { getTabIndex, handleKeyDown, refs } = useRovingTabIndex(tools.length);

  return (
    &lt;div role="toolbar" aria-label="Formatting tools"&gt;
      {tools.map((tool, i) =&gt; (
        &lt;button key={tool.id}
          ref={el =&gt; { refs.current[i] = el; }}
          tabIndex={getTabIndex(i)}
          onKeyDown={e =&gt; handleKeyDown(e, i)}
          aria-label={tool.label}
          aria-pressed={tool.active}&gt;
          {tool.icon}
        &lt;/button&gt;
      ))}
    &lt;/div&gt;
  );
}</pre>
      <p><strong>Focus management in modals:</strong> On open, focus the first focusable element. On close, return focus to the trigger element. Use <code>focus-trap-react</code> or <code>@radix-ui</code> primitives.</p>
      <p><strong>Skip links:</strong> Add a visually hidden "Skip to main content" link at the top of the page that becomes visible on focus, allowing keyboard users to bypass navigation.</p>
      <p><strong>Testing:</strong> Use <code>axe-core</code> / <code>@axe-core/react</code> in development for automated ARIA violation detection.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

      <p><strong>Architecture:</strong> Notification count stored in Redux/Zustand; updated via WebSocket push or polling. Badge renders derived count.</p>
<pre class="code-block">// notificationsSlice.ts
const notificationsSlice = createSlice({
  name: 'notifications',
  initialState: { items: [] as Notification[], unreadCount: 0 },
  reducers: {
    addNotification(state, action: PayloadAction&lt;Notification&gt;) {
      state.items.unshift(action.payload);
      if (!action.payload.read) state.unreadCount++;
    },
    markAllRead(state) {
      state.items.forEach(n =&gt; { n.read = true; });
      state.unreadCount = 0;
    },
  },
});

// WebSocket listener (in root component or middleware)
function NotificationListener() {
  const dispatch = useDispatch();
  useEffect(() =&gt; {
    const ws = new WebSocket('wss://api.example.com/notifications');
    ws.onmessage = (e) =&gt; dispatch(addNotification(JSON.parse(e.data)));
    return () =&gt; ws.close();
  }, [dispatch]);
  return null;
}

// Badge component
function NotificationBell() {
  const unreadCount = useSelector(s =&gt; s.notifications.unreadCount);
  return (
    &lt;button aria-label={`Notifications, ${unreadCount} unread`}&gt;
      🔔
      {unreadCount &gt; 0 &amp;&amp; (
        &lt;span className="badge" aria-hidden="true"&gt;
          {unreadCount &gt; 99 ? '99+' : unreadCount}
        &lt;/span&gt;
      )}
    &lt;/button&gt;
  );
}</pre>
      <p><strong>Browser tab badge:</strong> Update <code>document.title</code> to include the count (<code>"(3) App Name"</code>) so users see updates even when the tab is not active.</p>
      <p><strong>Browser Notifications API:</strong> For desktop push, request <code>Notification.requestPermission()</code> and use <code>new Notification(...)</code> to show OS-level notifications when the tab is not focused.</p>

  <div id="scenarios-q21" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q21-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">

      <p><strong>Options:</strong></p>
      <ul>
        <li><strong>Native browser:</strong> <code>&lt;iframe src="file.pdf"&gt;</code> — simplest, but no programmatic control.</li>
        <li><strong>react-pdf (pdfjs-dist):</strong> Renders each page to Canvas, full control, works everywhere.</li>
        <li><strong>Google Docs Viewer:</strong> Embed via iframe with a URL — no library needed, but requires public URL.</li>
      </ul>
<pre class="code-block">import { Document, Page, pdfjs } from 'react-pdf';
import 'react-pdf/dist/esm/Page/AnnotationLayer.css';

// Required: point pdfjs to its worker
pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = new URL(
  'pdfjs-dist/build/pdf.worker.min.js',
  import.meta.url,
).toString();

function PDFViewer({ url }: { url: string }) {
  const [numPages, setNumPages] = useState(0);
  const [page, setPage] = useState(1);
  const [scale, setScale] = useState(1.0);
  const containerRef = useRef&lt;HTMLDivElement&gt;(null);

  return (
    &lt;div ref={containerRef}&gt;
      &lt;div className="pdf-controls"&gt;
        &lt;button onClick={() =&gt; setPage(p =&gt; Math.max(1, p - 1))}&gt;Prev&lt;/button&gt;
        &lt;span&gt;{page} / {numPages}&lt;/span&gt;
        &lt;button onClick={() =&gt; setPage(p =&gt; Math.min(numPages, p + 1))}&gt;Next&lt;/button&gt;
        &lt;button onClick={() =&gt; setScale(s =&gt; s + 0.2)}&gt;Zoom In&lt;/button&gt;
        &lt;button onClick={() =&gt; setScale(s =&gt; Math.max(0.4, s - 0.2))}&gt;Zoom Out&lt;/button&gt;
      &lt;/div&gt;
      &lt;Document file={url} onLoadSuccess={({ numPages }) =&gt; setNumPages(numPages)}&gt;
        &lt;Page pageNumber={page} scale={scale} /&gt;
      &lt;/Document&gt;
    &lt;/div&gt;
  );
}</pre>
      <p><strong>Performance:</strong> Virtualise page rendering — only render the visible page plus one above/below. For large PDFs, lazy-load pages on scroll using IntersectionObserver. The pdfjs worker runs off the main thread so parsing doesn't block the UI.</p>
      <p><strong>Thumbnail sidebar:</strong> Render all pages at a very low scale (<code>scale=0.15</code>) in a scrollable sidebar. Click to jump to that page in the main viewer.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

<pre class="code-block">// Monaco Editor in React (via @monaco-editor/react)
import Editor, { OnMount } from '@monaco-editor/react';
import * as monaco from 'monaco-editor';
import { useRef } from 'react';

function CodeEditor({
  value, onChange, language = 'typescript'
}: {
  value: string;
  onChange: (v: string) =&gt; void;
  language?: string;
}) {
  const editorRef = useRef&lt;monaco.editor.IStandaloneCodeEditor | null&gt;(null);

  const handleMount: OnMount = (editor, monaco) =&gt; {
    editorRef.current = editor;

    // Add custom action: Ctrl+S to save
    editor.addAction({
      id: 'save',
      label: 'Save',
      keybindings: [monaco.KeyMod.CtrlCmd | monaco.KeyCode.KeyS],
      run: () =&gt; console.log('Save triggered'),
    });

    // Configure TypeScript language service
    monaco.languages.typescript.typescriptDefaults.setCompilerOptions({
      target: monaco.languages.typescript.ScriptTarget.ES2020,
      strict: true,
    });
  };

  return (
    &lt;Editor
      height="400px"
      language={language}
      value={value}
      onChange={v =&gt; onChange(v ?? '')}
      onMount={handleMount}
      options={{
        minimap: { enabled: false },
        fontSize: 14,
        lineNumbers: 'on',
        wordWrap: 'on',
        automaticLayout: true, // resizes on container change
      }}
    /&gt;
  );
}</pre>
      <p><strong>CodeMirror 6 pattern:</strong> More lightweight than Monaco. Build an EditorView in a <code>useEffect</code>, store it in a ref, and dispatch transactions to update value. Clean up with <code>view.destroy()</code> on unmount.</p>
      <p><strong>Performance:</strong> Monaco is ~4MB — load it lazily with <code>React.lazy</code> + Vite's dynamic import. The <code>@monaco-editor/react</code> loader handles this via CDN by default.</p>

<!-- Q23 -->
<div class="accordion-item">
  <h2 class="accordion-header" id="scenarios-q23-heading">
    <button class="accordion-button collapsed" type="button" data-bs-toggle="collapse" data-bs-target="#scenarios-q23" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="scenarios-q23">
      <span class="diff-scenario">Scenario</span>&nbsp; 23. How would you implement undo/redo for a drawing canvas?
    </button>
  </h2>
  <div id="scenarios-q23" class="accordion-collapse collapse" aria-labelledby="scenarios-q23-heading" data-bs-parent="#acc-scenarios">
    <div class="accordion-body">
      <p><strong>Pattern — immutable history stack:</strong> Store snapshots of the canvas state (list of shapes/strokes) in a past/future stacks. Each action pushes a new snapshot onto past.</p>
<pre class="code-block">interface HistoryState&lt;T&gt; {
  past: T[];
  present: T;
  future: T[];
}

function useHistory&lt;T&gt;(initial: T) {
  const [history, setHistory] = useState&lt;HistoryState&lt;T&gt;&gt;({
    past: [], present: initial, future: []
  });

  const set = useCallback((newPresent: T) =&gt; {
    setHistory(h =&gt; ({
      past: [...h.past, h.present],
      present: newPresent,
      future: [], // clear redo stack on new action
    }));
  }, []);

  const undo = useCallback(() =&gt; {
    setHistory(h =&gt; {
      if (h.past.length === 0) return h;
      const previous = h.past[h.past.length - 1];
      return {
        past: h.past.slice(0, -1),
        present: previous,
        future: [h.present, ...h.future],
      };
    });
  }, []);

  const redo = useCallback(() =&gt; {
    setHistory(h =&gt; {
      if (h.future.length === 0) return h;
      const next = h.future[0];
      return {
        past: [...h.past, h.present],
        present: next,
        future: h.future.slice(1),
      };
    });
  }, []);

  return { state: history.present, set, undo, redo,
           canUndo: history.past.length &gt; 0,
           canRedo: history.future.length &gt; 0 };
}

// In the canvas component
function DrawingCanvas() {
  const { state: strokes, set, undo, redo, canUndo, canRedo } =
    useHistory&lt;Stroke[]&gt;([]);

  function handleMouseUp(newStroke: Stroke) {
    set([...strokes, newStroke]); // commit completed stroke
  }

  useEffect(() =&gt; {
    const handleKey = (e: KeyboardEvent) =&gt; {
      if ((e.ctrlKey || e.metaKey) &amp;&amp; e.key === 'z') {
        e.shiftKey ? redo() : undo();
      }
    };
    window.addEventListener('keydown', handleKey);
    return () =&gt; window.removeEventListener('keydown', handleKey);
  }, [undo, redo]);
}</pre>
      <p><strong>Memory optimisation:</strong> Instead of storing full snapshots, store command objects (delta-based) and replay them forward/backward. Cap history depth (e.g., 50 steps).</p>
      <p><strong>Redux Toolkit alternative:</strong> <code>redux-undo</code> wraps any reducer with undo/redo for free.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

<pre class="code-block">import GridLayout, { Layout } from 'react-grid-layout';
import 'react-grid-layout/css/styles.css';
import 'react-resizable/css/styles.css';

const defaultLayout: Layout[] = [
  { i: 'sales', x: 0, y: 0, w: 6, h: 4 },
  { i: 'users', x: 6, y: 0, w: 6, h: 4 },
  { i: 'orders', x: 0, y: 4, w: 4, h: 3 },
];

function Dashboard() {

  // Persist layout changes
  const handleLayoutChange = (newLayout: Layout[]) =&gt; {
    setLayout(newLayout);
    localStorage.setItem('dashboardLayout', JSON.stringify(newLayout));
  };

  return (
    &lt;GridLayout
      layout={layout}
      cols={12}
      rowHeight={80}
      width={1200}
      onLayoutChange={handleLayoutChange}
      draggableHandle=".widget-handle"&gt;

      &lt;div key="sales"&gt;
        &lt;div className="widget-handle"&gt;⠿ Sales&lt;/div&gt;
        &lt;SalesChart /&gt;
      &lt;/div&gt;
      &lt;div key="users"&gt;
        &lt;div className="widget-handle"&gt;⠿ Users&lt;/div&gt;
        &lt;UsersChart /&gt;
      &lt;/div&gt;
    &lt;/GridLayout&gt;
  );
}</pre>
      <p><strong>Add/remove widgets:</strong> Manage a set of active widget IDs in state. Adding appends a new layout item with a default position. Removing filters it out.</p>
      <p><strong>Responsive breakpoints:</strong> Use <code>ResponsiveGridLayout</code> from <code>react-grid-layout</code> with separate layout configs per breakpoint (<code>lg</code>, <code>md</code>, <code>sm</code>).</p>
      <p><strong>Performance:</strong> Wrap each widget in <code>React.memo</code> — layout changes should not re-render widget content if data hasn't changed.</p>
